%DIF < %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%DIF < %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%% Description %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%DIF < %% This Latex file is the main file of the project. This means that it %%
%DIF < %% should be the one that is compiled. It is defining the document-    %%
%DIF < %% class, loads the packages from packages.tex, loads the custom       %%
%DIF < %% commands from commands.tex, defines the title page and loads        %%
%DIF < %% chapters from the chapter folder into the document. In the end it   %%
%DIF < %% is listing the references and loading any appendices necessary.     %%
%DIF < %%                                                                     %%
%DIF < %%                          IMPORTANT                                  %%
%DIF < %% If you want to add content to a chapter, add it to the individual   %%
%DIF < %% chapter files, not the main.tex file. This way, everything stays    %%
%DIF < %% organized.                                                          %%
%DIF < %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%DIF < %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%DIF -------

%DIF < \makeatletter

%DIF < \makeatother
%DIF -------
%for useful accronym, type \ac{ACR} to use, acronyms only show if called upon %DIF > 
% Added 'toc' option here if you want it in the Table of Contents,  %DIF > 
% otherwise remove it to silence the "Unused global option" warning if it was passed globally. %DIF > 
\usepackage[acronym]{glossaries}  %DIF > 
\makeglossaries %DIF > 
%don't let glossaries create its own heading %DIF > 
\renewcommand*{\glossarysection}[2][]{} %DIF > 
%DIF -------

%DIF 103-106c126-132
%DIF < %the following command implements roman numerals
%DIF < \makeatletter
%DIF < \newcommand*{\rom}[1]{\expandafter\@slowromancap\romannumeral #1@}
%DIF < \makeatother
%DIF -------
% Compact glossary style (reduces vertical space between entries) %DIF > 
\newglossarystyle{compactacronyms}{% %DIF > 
  \setglossarystyle{list}% %DIF > 
  \renewenvironment{theglossary}% %DIF > 
    {\begin{description}[itemsep=0pt, topsep=0pt, parsep=0pt, partopsep=0pt]}% %DIF > 
    {\end{description}}% %DIF > 
} %DIF >

%the following commands generate the same command as \ref{}, but with an added word in front.
\newcommand{\fref}[1]{Figure~\ref{#1}}
\newcommand{\tref}[1]{Table~\ref{#1}}
\newcommand{\cref}[1]{Chapter~\ref{#1}}
\newcommand{\sref}[1]{Section~\ref{#1}}
\newcommand{\aref}[1]{Appendix~\ref{#1}}

%the following command adds the functionality to easily highlight sth in the desired color. Use it like \hlc[color]{text}
\newcommand{\hlc}[2][yellow]{{\sethlcolor{#1}\hl{#2}}}

\newcommand{\dos}{\textcolor{red}}

\newsavebox{\DIFdelgraphicsbox} %DIF PREAMBLE
\newlength{\DIFdelgraphicswidth} %DIF PREAMBLE
\newlength{\DIFdelgraphicsheight} %DIF PREAMBLE
% store original definition of \includegraphics %DIF PREAMBLE
\LetLtxMacro{\DIFOincludegraphics}{\includegraphics} %DIF PREAMBLE
\providecommand{\DIFaddincludegraphics}[2][]{{\color{blue}\fbox{\DIFOincludegraphics[#1]{#2}}}} %DIF PREAMBLE
\providecommand{\DIFdelincludegraphics}[2][]{% %DIF PREAMBLE
\sbox{\DIFdelgraphicsbox}{\DIFOincludegraphics[#1]{#2}}% %DIF PREAMBLE
\settoboxwidth{\DIFdelgraphicswidth}{\DIFdelgraphicsbox} %DIF PREAMBLE
\settoboxtotalheight{\DIFdelgraphicsheight}{\DIFdelgraphicsbox} %DIF PREAMBLE
\scalebox{\DIFscaledelfig}{% %DIF PREAMBLE
\parbox[b]{\DIFdelgraphicswidth}{\usebox{\DIFdelgraphicsbox}\\[-\baselineskip] \rule{\DIFdelgraphicswidth}{0em}}\llap{\resizebox{\DIFdelgraphicswidth}{\DIFdelgraphicsheight}{% %DIF PREAMBLE
\setlength{\unitlength}{\DIFdelgraphicswidth}% %DIF PREAMBLE
\begin{picture}(1,1)% %DIF PREAMBLE
\thicklines\linethickness{2pt} %DIF PREAMBLE
{\color[rgb]{1,0,0}\put(0,0){\framebox(1,1){}}}% %DIF PREAMBLE
{\color[rgb]{1,0,0}\put(0,0){\line( 1,1){1}}}% %DIF PREAMBLE
{\color[rgb]{1,0,0}\put(0,1){\line(1,-1){1}}}% %DIF PREAMBLE
\end{picture}% %DIF PREAMBLE
}\hspace*{3pt}}} %DIF PREAMBLE
} %DIF PREAMBLE

%DIF > main text
\addchap{PREFACE}
\DIFaddend The REXUS/BEXUS programme is realised under a bilateral Agency Agreement between the German Aerospace Center (DLR) and the Swedish National Space Agency (SNSA). The Swedish share of the payload has been made available to students from other European countries through a collaboration with the European Space Agency (ESA). EuroLaunch, a cooperation between the Swedish Space Corporation (SSC) and the Mobile Rocket Base (MORABA) of DLR, is responsible for the campaign management and operations of the launch vehicles. Experts from DLR, SSC, ZARM and ESA provide technical support to the student teams throughout the project. REXUS and BEXUS are launched from SSC, Esrange Space Center in northern Sweden.

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend is an experiment developed by a team of students from the Uppsala Universitet in Sweden. Its aim is to demonstrate low-cost methane sensing capabilities using stratospheric balloons. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend is scheduled to fly aboard BEXUS as part of cycle 17 of the Swedish-German programme REXUS/BEXUS.

This document contains all relevant available information regarding \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{mirage}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend ; including the experiment's objectives and requirements, a breakdown of the experimental module's design, design verification procedures, a timeline and pre-launch campaign activities. Technical documents that pertain to the design are also included for reference, as appendix sections.\DIFaddbegin \newpage
\DIFaddend 

%DIF < %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%DIF < %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%% Abstract %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \chapter*{Abstract}
%DIFDELCMD < \markboth{Abstract}{Abstract}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{\DIFdel{Abstract}}
%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \addchap{ABSTRACT}
\DIFaddend 

Methane \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{is one of the most powerfull greenhouse gases contributing to climate change with about 25 times as much warming potential as carbondioxide over the span of one hundred years. To reduce the methane content in the atmosphere, it is highly important to understand methane sources and sinks. While a lot of methane is emitted by industries and waste sites, there are also natural emissions from, for example, wetlands. This shows the diverse environments in which monitoring is necessary. For this reason, current-day large-scale monitoring is done from space, relying on atmospheric models to calculate the methane concentration profile from the averaged column density. These atmospheric models require in-situ measurement data to make them more accurate. However, not many missions have done so for methane in the stratosphere, which makes the models less reliable overall and therefore renders monitoring less reliable as well. }\\
\DIFadd{Furthermore, commonly used laser-based technologies measuring methane with high precision are often very expensive and complex. This prevents more in-situ measurements from being recorded in the stratosphere.}\\  
\DIFadd{Methane }\DIFaddend InfraRed Absorption Gas Experiment (MIRAGE) aims to \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{demonstrate a low-cost, low-complexity alternative to laser-based technologies to }\DIFaddend measure stratospheric methane concentrations\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, }\DIFaddend using an off-the-shelf Non-Dispersive InfraRed (NDIR) sensor \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{. Current measurement techniques rely on laser-based setups, requiring fine adjustment while having a high cost. While these systems provide high resolution, they prevent frequent and cost-effective measurements. MIRAGE will demonstrate that NDIR sensors can fill the niche of low-cost measurements with reasonable resolution.
}%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{This is done by pressurizing }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{core. To increase the accuracy, }\DIFaddend temperature-controlled ambient air \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{is pressurised }\DIFaddend before feeding it into the optical chamber of the NDIR sensor. With this \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{setup it is expected to achieve an absolute concentration accuracy of $\mathrm{\Delta}c \leq 0.1$ ppm.
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{experiment, NDIR technology will be tested in regards to its limitations and future potential for use in atmospheric methane monitoring.
%DIF > This is done by pressurizing temperature-controlled ambient air before feeding it into the optical chamber of the NDIR sensor.
%DIF > With this setup it is expected to achieve an absolute concentration accuracy of \dos{$\mathrm{\Delta}c \leq 0.1$ ppm}.
}\DIFaddend 


%DIF < %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%DIF < %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%% Content %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%DIF > \dos{EXPAND THIS. Expansion is not a required action, but it was commented that our abstract is very short.}\newpage

\chapter{\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Introduction}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{INTRODUCTION}\DIFaddend }
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \label{sec:introduction}
\DIFaddend \section{Scientific/Technical Background}

Gases in the stratosphere play a pivotal role in climate modelling due to their prolonged lifetime.
Especially methane sources have been shown to play a big role in climate modelling \cite{stocker2013, saunois2017, nisbet2019, turner2019}\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, and the need of accurate measurements }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{. Since remote sensing via satellites is used to monitor methane sources and sinks on a large scale they contribute a lot to climate models. However, they heavily depend on atmospheric models to compute the methane concentrations at different altitudes from the averaged column densities they can measure. Therefore, more accurate in-situ measurements of methane are needed, which }\DIFaddend was reflected on in the National Research Council Decadal Survey for Earth Science \cite{national2019} and the summary report by the Carbon Climate Workshop in 2018 \cite{sellers2018}. 

The concentration of atmospheric methane ranges from around 2 ppm \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{down }\DIFaddend to 0.7 ppm \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{at }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{between }\DIFaddend 0 \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{km }\DIFdelend and 30 km altitude\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, respectively}\DIFdelend .
Because of the small concentrations, accurate optically complex systems like \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{tdlas} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{joly2020} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
or \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{ftir} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{tdlas} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{joly2020} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
or \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{ftir} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend \cite{runge2023} are widely employed.
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{tdlas} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{tdlas} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend systems send a laser beam of varying frequency close to the excitation energy of the target molecule through a gas sample and calculate the target molecule's concentration based on the measured absorption via the Beer-Lambert law.
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{ftir} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{ftir} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend works by sending a light beam containing multiple frequencies into the gas sample and recording the total absorption.
The frequencies are then changed and the process repeated.
This is often done via a Michelsen interferometer.
Both techniques \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{have the potential to }\DIFaddend enable great accuracy \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{but require high precision }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{depending on their path length. However, to get longer pathlengths it is often necessary to eflect the laser beam thousands of times since measurement are usually limited in space. Therefore, high precision is required }\DIFaddend in the complex optical setups, meaning that those systems are expensive\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and inaccessible }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, inaccessible and often highly sensitive to vibrations and shocks}\DIFaddend .

During recent years, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{ndir} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{ndir} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend sensors have advanced as a cost-effective and simple alternative to laser-based devices commonly employed for methane sensing.
NDIR spectroscopy works by passing a spectrum of \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{ir} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{ir} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend light through a gas sample where each gas absorbs the light at a unique wavelength.
An optical filter selects the wavelengths of the gas of interest.
The intensity of the transmitted light at the relevant wavelength can then be measured \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, and thus the change in intensity is known}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{to receive the absorbance $A=\log_{10}\left(\frac{I_0}{I}\right) = c\varepsilon l$}\DIFaddend .
The concentration c of the gas can then be calculated using the Beer-Lambert law

\begin{equation}
c = \log_{10}\left( \frac{I_{0}}{I} \right) \times {(\varepsilon l)}^{- 1},
\end{equation}

where $\varepsilon$ is the molar absorption coefficient, specific to the gas species, $l$ is the path length between light source and detector and $I_{0}$ and $I$ are the initial intensity of light and the intensity at the detector.
$I_{0}$ is determined either before the measurement or simultaneously using a second detector.
A schematic is provided in Figure \ref{fig:ndir_principle}.
Due to the simple setup, the overall cost of NDIR detectors is quite small with a range of tens to a few 100s of Euros. \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Furthermore, using a simple setup with a broad light sources, makes the device more robust against misalignment.
}\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{figure}[h]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \begin{figure}[htbp]
\DIFaddendFL \centering
\DIFdelbeginFL %DIFDELCMD < \includegraphics[width=8cm]{Graphics/Figures/NDIR schematic.png}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \includegraphics[width=8cm]{0_images/figures/NDIR schematic.png}
\DIFaddendFL \caption{Schematic of the non-dispersive infrared (NDIR) measurement principle.
Source: \cite{gaynullin2025}}
\label{fig:ndir_principle}
\end{figure}

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Since the pressure }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{At the same time, less reflections mean a shorter pathlength and a broader wavelength spectrum means limited applicability of the Beer-Lambert law. Another drawback of having a light source with a broader spectrum (compared to a laser) is that the absorption spectra of several molecules can overlap and make it harder to differentiate the effect of different absorbing molecules. In the case of methane, there is a large overlap with water molecules, which are usually present in a far bigger concentration in the atmosphere. This has previously limited NDIR so much that it couldn't be applied to measuring atmospheric methane. }\\
\begin{figure}[htbp]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=8cm]{0_images/figures/K96principle.png}
\caption{\DIFaddFL{Schematic of K96 sensor core, which combines three detectors for water, arbondioxide and methane.
Source: \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{wastine2022}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}}
\label{fig:K96_principle}
\end{figure}
\DIFadd{However, recently a new sensor has been developed by Senseair AB \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{wastine2022}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
, which measures $\mathrm{CH_4}$, $\mathrm{H_2 O}$, and $\mathrm{CO_2}$ at the same time by using three different detectors in one sensor core as depicted in }\autoref{fig:K96_principle}\DIFadd{. This allows one to subtract the influence of water and carbondioxide absorption from the methane signal. Therefore, this NDIR sensor is a promising candidate for atmospheric methane monitoring. }\\  
\DIFadd{While the K96 sensor is a state of the art sensor and delivers higher resolution methane measurements than other NDIR sensors, it is not quite accurate enough to measure atmospheric methane concentrations reliably. The \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{lod}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
, which gives the lowest concentration at atmospheric pressures that can be detected by the K96 sensor is about 3ppm\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{mao_improvement_2025}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
. Therefore, it is necessary to increase the concentration. Here it is important to differentiate the terms concentration and molar fraction, which are often used interchangeably because most contexts are working under ground level conditions with a constant pressure. While concentration gives the particle number per volume $c=\frac{n}{V}$, the molar fraction means particle number of a certain gas species per total particle number including all present gas species $x_i=\frac{n_i}{n_{tot}}$. When a detector resolution is given in particles-per-million or ppm, this is usually assumed for ground level. In reality the quantity of interest for an optical sensor that is based on the Beer-Lambert law is the concentration of the gas species.}\\ 
\DIFadd{Now, since the pressure }\DIFaddend $p$ decreases exponentially with altitude, the concentration

\begin{equation}
c = \frac{n}{V}
\end{equation}

connected to the pressure by the ideal gas law

\begin{equation}
pV = nRT
\end{equation}

with the volume $V$, the ideal gas constant $R$ and the temperature $T$, decreases with about the same rate as the pressure. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{At the same time the }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{If it were assumed that the composition of the air stayed constant, the molar fraction would not be affected by this drop in the particle number. However, the emitted light would now encounter way fewer particles and therefore be less absorbed. This means that a detector with low accuracy has an even lower signal if the pressure drops. Furthermore, the }\DIFaddend relative molar fraction of methane molecules compared to other molecules in the air is \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{decreasing}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{actually decreasing from 2\,ppm to about 1\,ppm as the atmospheric composition changes between Troposphere and Stratosphere}\DIFaddend , which means that there are \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{very little }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{even fewer }\DIFaddend methane molecules at the altitudes \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we can reach.This needs to be considered when working with a sensor offering lower resolution. }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{eached by the BEXUS gondola.}\\
\DIFadd{Therefore it is necessary to pressurise the air to increase the concentration of methane particles. Due to the \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{lod} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
of the K96 of 3\,ppm it is not enough to keep the pressure at 1\,bar. Instead it is necessary to increase the pressure to at least 3\,bar to be able to measure with the K96 even at altitudes of 20\,km where the molar fraction could be already as low as 1\,ppm. Having a pressure of 3 bar in the measurement chamber would increase the "effective molar fraction" to 3\,ppm in that case, just high enough to rely on the sensor. }\\
\DIFadd{The sensor is susceptible to other factors causing drift such as temperature and humidity. These will require a thorough calibration strategy, which allows to measure the methane concentration under varying conditions. An AI-based calibration approach has been tested before on the K96 sensor\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{gia_accurate_2025} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
and therefore a similar approach could be employed for \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
. At the same time, the experiment should limit the temperature range of the air to be measured, which requires a thermal control system.}\\
\DIFaddend 



%DIF > %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Mission Statement}

As explained in Section 1.1 methane measurements are of great importance for climate modelling.
However, systems with which methane measurements are taken, are oftentimes expensive and complex in setup.
Therefore, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{our mission is }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
aims }\DIFaddend to demonstrate a low-cost, low-complexity solution for measuring methane concentrations in the upper stratosphere.
By using the novel K96 non-dispersive infrared (NDIR) sensor developed by Senseair \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{AB }\DIFaddend (a Swedish company, specialised in state-of-the-art gas sensors) \cite{wastine2022} \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we will use }\DIFdelend off-the-shelf technology \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{will be shown }\DIFaddend to provide an alternative to laser-based approaches.

%DIF > %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

%DIF > %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Experiment Concept}

The Non-Dispersive Infra-Red (NDIR) sensor detects light absorption due to the number of absorbing particles in the optical cavity within a narrow wavelength range.
As mentioned in Section 1.1, this number is related to the concentration of the contributing gas species and their pressures and temperature.
Thus, it is possible to increase the concentration of a gas species by increasing the pressure of the gas while maintaining the same relative composition and molar fractions of the sample.

Therefore, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we use }\DIFdelend an NDIR sensor fed with pressurized ambient air under temperature-controlled conditions \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{will be used. To keep a pressure of 3\,bar up to at least 20\,km altitude is the real challenge of \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
. As explained above, ambient air needs to be pressurized to 3 bar using a combination of vaccuum pumps and a compressor, that work together. Vaccuum pumps are meant to draw in low density ambient air and pre-pressurise this air to provide air dense enough for the compressor to further pressurise it to 3 bar}\DIFaddend . \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The measurement resolution of the sensor is 0.1 ppm at ground level, i.e. at 1 bar . Because the uncertainty we aim for is less than 0.1 ppm, we need to pressurize the ambient air to 2 to 5 bar . Thus, we aim to use a pump to continuously pump ambient air into a pressurized chamber, in which the sensor is located. }\DIFdelend Air can leave the pressurized chamber through \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{an electrical valve. This method of active air release can restrict the flow rate dynamically, adjusting to the pressure measured internally. }%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{As the detector output can drift with temperature, we need to }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{a valve, which could be passive since the outflow rate is independent of altitude since it is limited by the speed of sound even if the pressure difference is just 2 bar as it will be on ground level. The concept and different components involved in the pressurisation system will be explained in more depth in the mechanical design section below. }\\
\DIFadd{To }\DIFaddend stabilize the temperature \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{of the air is another complex challenge, that needs to be solved }\DIFaddend via a thermal control system\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{. Additionally, we need information }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, that can handle varying ambient conditions. The air is initially very cold with a low density but due to pressurisation it can heat up substantially. At the same time, it's mass is small and it will lose heat to surrounding tubing and chamber walls. Electrical components such as pumps, that are also generating heat and active and passive heating elements need to make sure that the air is cooled and heated to the right temperatures in the right places. An extensive thermal study including more factors will analyse the thermal system needed further in the thermal design section below.}\\
\DIFadd{Additionally, information is needed }\DIFaddend about the ambient pressure and temperature, to inform the thermal control system and the flow rate of the pumps. \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Furthermore, this allows for calculation of the concentration of the methane particles outside of the experiment from the concentration measured via the ideal gas law.}\\
\DIFaddend As water vapor is a major factor in the uncertainty of the sensor \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, we also need to monitor }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{and condensation of water could damage the sensor and other electronics, }\DIFaddend the inside and ideally outside humidity \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{should be monitored as well}\DIFaddend .
These measurements can then be used to engage mitigation methods like \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{stopping of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{closing the vent, stopping }\DIFaddend the pumps and raising \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{of }\DIFdelend the internal temperature to \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{prevent }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{increase the water capacity of the air and prevent further }\DIFaddend condensation. Once the ambient humidity sensor is reporting safe levels, the \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{pressurisation system can start working again, flushing out the more humid air. The }\DIFaddend internal temperature is to be set to normal operating conditions \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, and the pumps commence a full flushing cycle. This means that the pumps operate with the maximum flow rate for 2 minutes. Afterwards, the internal humidity levels are measured. If they are too high, another flushing cycle commences up to a total of 3 cycles, after which normal operations start again. }%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{Processing of the different sensor outputs and engaging of appropriate actions will be done via a \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{mcu} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
like an Arduino Nano.  
}%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{again as well. }\\
\DIFadd{Many sensors will be required to monitor those different ambient conditions and internal temperature, pressure and humidity. Depending on the location within the setup they need to be able to work under different conditions and fulfill different accuracy and range requirements. An analysis of their selection and the state of the art is done in the electrical design section below.}\\
\DIFadd{A \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mcu} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
will be integrated into a PCB designed to handle all of the different processes that the experiment has to fulfill to ensure reliable measurements of the atmospheric methane concentrations up to an altitude of at least 20\,km.  
}\DIFaddend A block diagram showcasing the different functional/physical experiment blocks is provided below in Figure \ref{fig:block_diagram}.

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{figure}[h]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \begin{figure}[t]
\DIFaddendFL \centering
\DIFdelbeginFL %DIFDELCMD < \includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{Graphics/Figures/Components block diagram.png}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{0_images/figures/Components block diagram.png}
\DIFaddendFL \caption{Block diagram with different physical or functional components of the experiment.}
\label{fig:block_diagram}
\end{figure}

H. }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{1.5}\degree \DIFadd{C. }\DIFaddend \\

\DIFdel{C.}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{below 90\% r.H. }\DIFaddend \\
\hline
P\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{.10 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{.11.1 }\DIFaddend & The experiment \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{should keep the temperature of the air inside the measurement chamber within }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{shall measure the humidity inside of the measurement chamber in }\DIFaddend a range of \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{19 and 23}%DIFDELCMD < \degree %%%
\DIFdel{C.}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{0 to 100\% r.H. }\DIFaddend \\
\hline
P.11\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{.2 }\DIFaddend & The experiment shall \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{keep }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{measure }\DIFaddend the humidity inside of the measurement chamber \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{below 90}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{with a maximum uncertainty of 3}\DIFaddend \% r.H. \\
\hline
P.12 & The experiment should measure the temperature, pressure and humidity inside of the measurement chamber at a rate \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{of 10Hz}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{over 10 Hz}\DIFaddend . \\
\hline
P.13.1 & The \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{ndir} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
sensor shall have a measurement time for the CH4, CO2 and H2O concentrations of 20s during ascent and descent. }%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < \hline
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{P.13.2 }%DIFDELCMD < & %%%
\DIFdel{The \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{ndir} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
sensor shall have a measurement time for the CH4, CO2 and H2O concentrations of 50s during the floating phase. }%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < \hline
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{P.14.1 }%DIFDELCMD < & %%%
\DIFdel{The }\DIFdelend experiment should measure the ambient pressure outside in a range of 20 to 1100 mbar. \\
\hline
P\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{.14}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{.13}\DIFaddend .2 & The experiment should measure the ambient pressure outside with a maximum uncertainty of \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{0.05 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{20 }\DIFaddend mbar. \\
\hline
P\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{.15}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{.14}\DIFaddend .1 & The experiment should measure the ambient temperature outside in a range of \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{-100 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{-70 }\DIFaddend to +60 \degree C. \\
\hline
P\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{.15}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{.14}\DIFaddend .2 & The experiment should measure the ambient temperature outside with a maximum uncertainty of 1.5\degree C. \\
\hline
P\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{.16}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{.15}\DIFaddend .1 & The experiment should measure the ambient humidity outside in a range of 0 to 100\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\% }\DIFaddend r.H. \\
\hline
P\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{.16}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{.15}\DIFaddend .2 & The experiment should measure the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{humidity outside the sensor box }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{ambient humidity outside }\DIFaddend with a maximum uncertainty of 3\% r.H. \\
\hline
P\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{.17 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{.16 }\DIFaddend & The experiment should measure the ambient temperature, pressure and humidity outside at a rate \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{of 10Hz}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{over 10 Hz}\DIFaddend . \\
\hline
P\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{.18 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{.17 }\DIFaddend & The experiment should receive data via E-Link with an uplink rate \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{of 10kbps}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{under 10 kbps}\DIFaddend . \\
\hline
P\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{.19 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{.18 }\DIFaddend & The experiment shall send the obtained data with the E-Link with a downlink rate \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{under }\DIFaddend 100 kbps. \\

\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{A Gantt chart has been made to visualize the work to be done and the duration of specific tasks. It was divided into the different subteams in addition to a system wide \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{ait}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
. The Gantt chart is shown in \fref{fig:gantt}, with the critical path highlighted in red.
}\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The Gannt chart in \fref{fig:gannt} shows the general schedule of the project}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The critical path is Define Scientific Objectives - Define Requirements - Order Materials - Build Pressurized Chamber. This demonstrates the importance of the pressurized chamber on the whole experiment and thus the project planning.
}

\DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
team members have declared their availability per week throughout the project duration, so that certain people were assigned different tasks.
}

\DIFadd{OnlineGantt was used to manage scheduling and assigning the tasks, whereas Discord is used for communications within the team}\DIFaddend .
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Due to several dates being uncertain yet, it was approximated accross a longer period.
The color coding represents the responsible subteam.
}\DIFdelend

%DIF >  %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\DIFaddend \section{Resources}

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend is a project conducted by the RiseUpp association, which is under the umbrella of Astronomisk Ungdom. The RiseUpp association has a dedicated outreach team working on finding sponsors. Currently \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend is the only project RiseUpp is working on, therefore a majority of this budget will go to \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{mirage}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend .

As part of Astronomisk Ungdom, RiseUpp get annually 2000 SEK and 20 SEK per member. RiseUpp aims to be an association at Uppsala university that gathers all students interested in space, hosts events such as lunch lectures, and participate in programmes like Rexus Bexus.

The \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend project will consist mostly of students working on their thesis, therefore Uppsala university \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{provides }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{covers costs up to }\DIFaddend 1000 SEK per student. In addition, through \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{our }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{the team's }\DIFaddend supervisor, Uwe Zimmermann, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we have }\DIFdelend access to a laboratory with the necessary tools and a vacuum chamber for testing \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{is given}\DIFaddend . Uppsala university also hosts the Swedish Institute for Space Physics (Institutet för Rymdfysik), which has a thermal chamber that \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we will be using }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{will be used }\DIFaddend for testing.

RiseUpp has an agreement with the Swedish company \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, SenseAir }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{SenseAir AB}\DIFaddend , in which SenseAir \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{has provided }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{AB has provided a brand new K96 sensor, a used K96 sensor for testing, \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{ir} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
lamps (which are a critical part of }\DIFaddend the K96 sensor\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{) }\DIFaddend and will provide extra gas sensors if needed.

\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{In addition, the sensor calibrations will be done in collaboration with the Norunda weather stations; who will provide gas samples and a Picarro gas analyzer for reference.
}

\DIFadd{The gas pumps and the compressor are purchased and received, which is another crucial component to the mission.
}

%DIF >  %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\DIFaddend \subsection{Workforce}

The workforce consists of voluntary and thesis students. Voluntary students spend around 10 hours a week and will be the main workforce until March, they do this voluntarily and will be the core team members. Thesis students \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{will be }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{are }\DIFaddend recruited to begin working on the project from March, they will work in project groups under the supervision of \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{our }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{the team's }\DIFaddend supervisor, Associate Professor Uwe Zimmermann, and will get credited for the work. The thesis \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{project }\DIFaddend will be 15 credits, and the students are expected to work full-time on the project \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{from 23rd of March until the 5th of June}\DIFaddend .

\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{More information about the thesis projects is shown in \tref{tab:thesis}. Thesis students will not directly write into the \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{sed} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
but they will write their own university reports.
}

\DIFadd{One task for the voluntary students is to mentor and follow up with the thesis students. The voluntary students cover all subteams and will act as the interface between the thesis projects and the \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
project.
}

\DIFadd{There are weekly meetings for the whole team in which the core team members will follow up closely with the thesis projects and update on the progress, in addition to an extra subteam meeting each week to work on given tasks and plan the next steps. Thesis students will have the chance, and be encouraged, to continue working on the project voluntarily.
}

\begin{table}[htbp]
\centering
\caption{\DIFaddFL{Thesis Projects Overview}}
\label{tab:thesis}
\begin{tabular}{|l|L{3.5cm}|L{5.5cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Project Number} & \textbf{Project Name} & \textbf{Project Description} \\ \hline

1 & Finite Element Analysis (FEA) and Computational Fluid Dynamics (CFD) 
& Finite Element Analysis (FEA) of temperature and stress \& Computational Fluid Dynamics (CFD) to analyze airflow. 
\\ \hline

2 & PCB Design and Embedded Programming 
& Printed circuit board (PCB) design, component selection, and embedded programming. 
\\ \hline

3 & Pressurized Gas Sensing Compartment 
& Design and assembly of a pressurized gas sensing experiment compartment. 
 \\ \hline

4 & Data Analysis Pipeline 
& Data analysis pipeline programming. 
 \\ \hline

5 & NDIR Sensor Testing and Calibration 
& Sensor testing and calibration of an NDIR gas sensor for stratospheric pressure and temperature conditions. 
 \\ \hline

6 & Thermal System Design 
& Thermal system design. 
 \\ \hline

7 & ECSS-Based Material Selection 
& Material selections in accordance with ECSS guidelines for a leakage-free and heat-resistant compartment. 
 \\ \hline

8 & Power Distribution Board Design 
& Power distribution board design. 
\\ \hline

\end{tabular}
\end{table}

}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD

%DIF >  %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsection{Budget}

The estimated total budget of the experiment \DIFdelbegin \textit{\DIFdel{parts}} %DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{only with a 10}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \emph{\DIFadd{parts}} \DIFadd{without the K96 sensor is 6089 SEK, and with a 15}\DIFaddend \% buffer is \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{9500 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{7000 }\DIFaddend SEK ($\approx$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{900 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{650 }\DIFaddend EUR). \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{However, the }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The }\DIFaddend K96 sensor, which \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we got }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{was }\DIFaddend sponsored, is not commercially available and was estimated to be 5000 SEK\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{; making the total cost of the experiment around 1200 EUR}\DIFaddend . Additional managerial costs like outreach and travel expenses lead to a sum of approximately \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{90000 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{85000 }\DIFaddend SEK ($\approx$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{8500 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{8000 }\DIFaddend EUR).

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{longtable}{p{3cm}p{1.7cm}p{2cm}p{1.5cm}p{5cm}}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{For the hardware, \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
was sponsored by SenseAir AB and received 2 K96 sensors; one for testing and one for use. Additionally, the pumps and the compressor were ordered.
}

\DIFadd{All of the hardware costs can be covered by the money given through Uppsala university for the thesis projects, however \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
aims to find external sponsors for additional outreach budget. Additional material such as cables, screws, RTCs and small microcontrollers are available for the team in the designated lab at Uppsala university and is provided; they were not added to the total cost.
}

\subsection{External Support}

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend is endorsed and adviced by the Uppsala university department of meteorology. In addition, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend is in the process of becoming an associated association to the student union for science and engineering at Uppsala university (UTN). This will open up the doors to apply for research grants provided by the UTN. Astronomisk Ungdom has a research grant pool of 100000 SEK which is available for associations under their umbrella, which will be applied to.

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We are }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
is }\DIFaddend in talks with Uppsala University Innovation and the development office at the university about financial and outreach support. They will connect \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{us }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend with companies that work in the field and help \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{us }\DIFdelend with social events organized by RiseUpp.

\DIFdelbegin \section{\DIFdel{Outreach Approach}}
%DIFAUXCMD
\addtocounter{section}{-1}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelend %DIF >  %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
RexusBexus team will contact local news agencies, such as Uppsala Nya Tidning, Techna (student university magazine) and appear on Student radio (local independent radiostation).
The team also aims to apear on Uppsala University website. 
The RiseUpp association is under the Astronomisk Ungdom association and a website will be ran under their domain. A project documentary movie will follow the Rexus }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \section{\DIFadd{Outreach Approach}}
\subsection{\DIFadd{Goal of the outreach}}
\DIFadd{The aim is to spread the word of the Rexus}\DIFaddend /Bexus \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{team as they work on the project and will document the flight. }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{programme and MIRAGE to as large an audiance as possible. Especially inspiring STEM majors at Uppsala university to engage in MIRAGE or similar Rexus/Bexus projects and experiments in the future.
}\vspace{3mm}\\
\DIFadd{The MIRAGE team has advertised themselves by posting continuous updates on social media about the experiment, team meetings, team building activities and humorous content. They have also written an informative letter about the Rexus Bexus programme, the RiseUpp association and MIRAGE that has been announced on several engineering program's studium pages for recruitment of bachelor thesis students.
}\vspace{3mm}\\
\DIFadd{Other media sources that the team has advertised themselves via, are newspapers. An article was written in the students university´s magazine Techna.
}\vspace{3mm}\\
\DIFadd{To cover equipment costs for the experiment and travel expenses the team has contacted local and national STEM-companies, authorities and foundations to ask for sponsorships and collaborations. One foundation that has been contacted was Sparbanksstiftelsen Upland, Swedbank and the team have an ongoing collaboration with RedBull.
}\DIFaddend

\DIFaddbegin \subsection{\DIFadd{Future outreach plans}}
\DIFadd{In the future, the team plans to arrange lunch lectures with SSC, Christer Fuglesang, Marcus Wandt. These events can be sponsored by Uppsala kommun and supported by RedBull to attract a greater audience.

}\vspace{3mm}\\
\DIFadd{In a later stage of the project, a documentary movie will be released that follows the team´s project journey and the launch from Kiruna in October 2026.
}



\DIFaddend \section{Risk Register}

\textbf{Risk ID}

TC -- technical/implementation

MS -- mission (operational performance)

SF -- safety

VE -- vehicle

PE -- personnel

EN -- environmental

OR -- organisational

DS -- data related

\textbf{Probability (P)}

A. Minimum -- Almost impossible to occur

B. Low -- Small chance to occur

C. Medium -- Reasonable chance to occur

D. High -- Quite likely to occur

E. Maximum -- Certain to occur, maybe more than once

\textbf{Severity (S)}

1. Negligible -- Minimal or no impact

2. Significant -- Leads to reduced experiment performance

3. Major -- Leads to failure of subsystem or loss of flight data

4. Critical -- Leads to experiment failure or creates minor health hazards

5. Catastrophic -- Leads to termination of the REXUS and/or BEXUS programme, damage to the vehicle or injury to personnel

The rankings for probability (P) and severity (S) are combined to assess the overall risk classification, ranging from very low to very high and being coloured green, yellow, orange or red according to the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\ac{sed} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{sed} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFaddend guidelines.

\begin{longtable}{L{1.5cm}L{3cm}L{1cm}L{1cm}L{2cm}L{6cm}}
\caption{Risk Register}
\label{tab:risk_register}\\

\toprule
\textbf{ID} & \textbf{Risk \& consequence} & \textbf{P} & \textbf{S} &
\textbf{P x S} & \textbf{Prevention and/or Mitigation Action} \\
\midrule
\endfirsthead

\toprule
\textbf{ID} & \textbf{Risk \& consequence} & \textbf{P} & \textbf{S} &
\textbf{P x S} & \textbf{Prevention and/or Mitigation Action} \\
\midrule
\endhead

\multicolumn{6}{r}{\textit{Continued on next page}}\\
\endfoot

\bottomrule
\endlastfoot

\DIFaddend \rowcolor{mediumorange} MS10 & \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Over frozen }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Over-frozen }\DIFaddend gas inlet or outlet & C & 4 & medium & Large enough radius \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{of outlets and inlets}\DIFaddend , heating element at inlet \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and warm }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{to heat }\DIFaddend air to appropriate temperature\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, move primary expansion point of air to being inside the experiment enclosure }\DIFaddend \\

\DIFaddend \rowcolor{lowyellow} TC30 & Failure of thermal control \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{due to too low temperatures }\DIFaddend & \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{C }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{B }\DIFaddend & 3 & low & \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Testing and simulations, more heating or cooling depending on results }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Acceptable risk}\DIFaddend \\
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \rowcolor{lowyellow} %%%

\rowcolor{mediumorange} OR10 & Lack of funding & \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{B }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{C }\DIFaddend & \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{5 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{4 }\DIFaddend & medium & \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Contacting of companiesin progress }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Contact more companies, find other sources from university }\DIFaddend \\
\rowcolor{lowyellow} \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{OR11 }& \DIFadd{Lack of funding }& \DIFadd{B }& \DIFadd{4 }& \DIFadd{low }& \DIFadd{Acceptable risk  }\\

\DIFdelbegin \chapter{\DIFdel{Experiment Description}}
%DIFAUXCMD
\addtocounter{chapter}{-1}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelend %DIF >  %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%\newpage

\DIFaddbegin \chapter{\DIFadd{EXPERIMENT DESCRIPTION}}
\label{sec:experiment_description}
\DIFaddend \section{Experiment \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Setup}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{setup}\DIFaddend }

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{figure}[h]
%DIFDELCMD <     %%%
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \begin{figure}[htbp]
    \DIFaddendFL \centering
    \DIFdelbeginFL %DIFDELCMD < \includegraphics[width=0.8\textwidth]{Graphics/Figures/Mirage Block schematic.png}
%DIFDELCMD <     %%%
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \includegraphics[width=0.8\textwidth]{0_images/figures/Mirage Block schematic.png}
    \DIFaddendFL \caption{Experimental Setup}
    \label{fig:experimental_setup}

\end{figure}

The experiment will feature a NDIR sensor (K96), a pressurization system, a thermal system, ambient environment sensors and a processing unit. 
The pressurization system will include a pumping mechanism in order to increase the pressure and the amount of particles \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we can measure. The gas }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{that can be measured. The air }\DIFaddend will be heated up and pumped into the measurement chamber with the K96 sensor inside together with temperature, pressure and humidity sensors. The gas will be exchanged continously to exchange the sample while maintaining the pressure of \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{at least 2 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{3 }\DIFaddend bar. 
The K96 Sensor will communicate with the processing unit and the processing unit sends the measured digital data for storage to the SDHC card.
The pressure sensor,temperature sensor and humidity sensor communicate with the processing unit via digital interfaces (such as $I^2C$) to ensure that the pump and thermal control system are running with the right parameters to maintain room temperature conditions and a stable pressure \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{between 2 and 5 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{of 3 }\DIFaddend bar. Unique addresses are used to identify each sensor's signal, allowing the processing unit to collect and organize data from all ambient sensors efficiently.

%DIF > %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Experiment Interfaces}

%DIF > %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsection{Mechanical \DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \MBLOCKRIGHTBRACE
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{The experiment is mounted }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Interface}}\label{mechanical_interface}

\DIFadd{The \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
enclosure is mechanically attached }\DIFaddend to the ESCARGO \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{aluminium frame composed of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{gondola structure via four mounting points located on its bottom plate. These four connection points interface with two parallel }\DIFaddend 45 $\times$ 45 \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{~mm Bosch-type }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{mm Bosch aluminium }\DIFaddend T-slot profiles \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{used by the BEXUS gondola.
}%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{The experiment is housed in a rigid aluminium enclosure and is fixed to a structural aluminium base plate using vertical }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{using }\DIFaddend M6 \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{bolts. The base plate forms the primary load-bearing interface of the experiment and ensures a rigid connection between the experiment enclosure and the gondola mounting structure. }%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{The aluminium base plate is attached }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{T-bolts, M6 rubber spacers, and M6 flange nuts. The parallel profiles are then mounted }\DIFaddend to the ESCARGO \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{frame via horizontal }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{gondola structure using standard Rexroth }\DIFaddend M6 \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{bolts engaging }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{brackets, }\DIFaddend M6 \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{T-nuts (or }\DIFdelend T-bolts\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{) inserted into the ESCARGO T-slots. The horizontal bolt orientation allows direct fastening }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, and M6 flange nuts. This configuration facilitates installation without necessitating structural modifications }\DIFaddend to the ESCARGO \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{profiles without any modification of the gondola structure.
Washers are used under all bolt heads to ensure proper load distribution}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{frame, ensuring full compatibility with the standard mounting interface.
}

\DIFadd{To reduce vibration transmission, temperature transfer and accommodate minor alignment tolerances during installation, rubber spacers are installed between the enclosure and the mounting brackets}\DIFaddend .

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{A total of four independent mounting points are used between the base plate }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The mounting configuration provides a rigid mechanical interface between the experiment enclosure }\DIFaddend and the ESCARGO frame, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{providing redundancy and ensuring that the experiment remains securely attached in the event of a single fastener failure}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{ensuring structural redundancy and compliance with the standard ESCARGO mechanical interface requirements}\DIFaddend .

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{No modifications to the ESCARGO frame are required. A schematic diagram of the mechanical interface between the experiment, the aluminium base plate, and the ESCARGO frame is provided.
}%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \begin{table}[h]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \begin{table}[htbp]
\DIFaddendFL \centering
\DIFdelbeginFL %DIFDELCMD < \caption{%
{%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelFL{Mechanical interface fasteners and mounting hardware}}
%DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < \begin{tabular}{|l|c|l|}
%DIFDELCMD < \hline
%DIFDELCMD < \textbf{Item} & \textbf{Quantity} & \textbf{Specification} \\

%DIFDELCMD < Bolts (experiment $\rightarrow$ base plate) & 4 & M6, steel \\

\DIFdelbeginFL \subsection{\DIFdelFL{Electrical}}
%DIFAUXCMD
\addtocounter{subsection}{-1}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \end{figure}
%DIF > %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsection{\DIFadd{Electrical Interface}}\label{electrical_interface}
\DIFaddend 

\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The electrical interface to the Bexus power unit consists of the MIL-C 26482P series 1 connector, as provided by the user manual. Using pin A and B, the supply voltage from the SAFT MP176065 battery pack will be fed to the power distribution board.
The connector to the E-Link of the gondola will be an Amphenol RJF21B and the RJ45 connector will be employed for communication with a RJ45 plug on the MCU PCB.
}

\DIFaddend Since the Bexus power supply is 28.8V \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we will use }\DIFdelend two LM2596HVS step-down voltage regulators \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{on our }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{will be used on the }\DIFaddend power distribution board. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We will use }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{For the MCU and K96 sensor }\DIFaddend 8V \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{for our Arduino, pressurization system }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{will be used, the pressurization system operates at 24V, the thermal system at 12V }\DIFaddend and \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{K96 sensor, and }\DIFdelend 3.3V for the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{ambient sensors. Our estimated }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{sensors. The estimated average }\DIFaddend current draw from the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{power distribution board without the thermal system is 1.15A , which is well below the max current of 3A for the step-down voltage regulators. Regarding our current draw from the Bexus power unit , we estimate 0.35A. The thermal system is still not worked out and }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{BEXUS battery is 0.8A and the average power consumption is 23.11W. The total power consumption from BEXUS power unit }\DIFaddend is \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{therefore not in the calculations}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{138.67Wh as listed in section 4.7 and the peak current draw is 2.26A. For protecting the BEXUS batteries and other experiments a pre-charge circuit will be implemented in order to limit the currents of the pressurization system and an LC filter to deal with the EMI and switching frequencies of DC/DC converters}\DIFaddend . Distributed single point ground will be implemented.


\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{figure}[H]
%DIFDELCMD <     \centering
%DIFDELCMD <     \includegraphics[width=1.0\textwidth]{Graphics/Figures/Skarmbild.png}
%DIFDELCMD <     %%%
%DIFDELCMD < \caption{%
{%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelFL{Electrical Schematic}}
    %DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < \label{fig:electrical_schematic}
%DIFDELCMD < \end{figure}
%DIFDELCMD <

%DIFAUXCMD

%DIFDELCMD < \begin{tabular}{llp{8cm}}

\DIFdelend %DIF > %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsection{Thermal}\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{The thermal properties of our }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \label{thermal}
\DIFadd{As outlined in \sref{sec: thermal design}, the thermal behaviour of the }\DIFaddend experiment will be \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{partially controlled by heating /cooling elements . The specifics remain to be determined once the thermal behaviour of the electronic components can be modelled or tested. Where necessary, we will insulate the whole experiment to avoid an impact of the extreme temperatures, which can go down to -80}%DIFDELCMD < \degree %%%
\DIFdel{C, on the electronics and pumps. This will be also done by rubber bumpers to avoid cooling from the gondola, therefore also mitigating heat transfer to the gondola .
}%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{The thermal impact on the vehicle should be minimal, but this }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{controlled via heating elements and insulation. To avoid thermal coupling to ESCARGO, rubber bumpers between the experiment and the gondola will be used.
The thermal coupling }\DIFaddend will be further tested when \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we have all components}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{the experiment is assembled}\DIFaddend . The air inlet and outlet for the air samples to be measured will be directed away from the vehicle and should not heat or cool the vehicle\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{either}\DIFdelend .

%DIF > %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Experiment Components}

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\caption{Experiment summary table}

%DIF > %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Mechanical Design}\DIFaddbegin \label{mechanical_design}
\DIFaddend 

The mechanical design of the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{experiment consists of an external protective aluminium housing with dimensions of 100x100x50 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
experiment focuses on a compact enclosure housing a pressurized measurement chamber, a multi-stage pump system, supporting electronics, and a heating system. \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
is designed to fit within the ESCARGO gondola structure while maintaining structural integrity and ensuring safe operation under the environmental conditions expected during the mission.
}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
    \centering
    \includegraphics[width=0.8\textwidth]{0_images/figures/tech_drawing.png}
    \caption{\DIFaddFL{Technical drawing of the system as a whole.}}
    \label{fig:tech_drawing}

\end{figure}

\subsection{\DIFadd{Experiment Enclosure}}

\DIFadd{The experiment is housed in a \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{cots} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
aluminium enclosure with external dimensions of $200\times 200\times 150$ }\DIFaddend mm and a wall thickness of \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{expected }\DIFaddend 2 mm\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, as well as an internal pressurised chamber with dimensions of 38x33x45 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{. The enclosure provides mechanical protection for all internal components and acts as the primary structural body of the experiment. A \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{cots} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
enclosure was selected to reduce manufacturing complexity, minimize cost, and provide a robust structural housing with well-characterized mechanical properties.
The enclosure is directly mounted to the ESCARGO frame as described in \sref{mechanical_interface}. Internally, the enclosure accommodates the pressure chamber, two diaphragm vacuum pumps, one piston compressor, a passive outflow hole, shutter valve, tubing, and electronic control hardware. The enclosure also includes two dedicated holes for air inlet and one for outlet, as well as electrical feedthroughs required for connecting to the BEXUS power and E-link system.
}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
    \centering
    \includegraphics[width=0.45\textwidth]{0_images/figures/tech_drawing_3.png}
    \includegraphics[width=0.45\textwidth]{0_images/figures/tech_drawing_5.png}
    \caption{\DIFaddFL{Technical drawings of experiment enclosure. Drawings are representative and the thickness of both “Main Body” and “Main Lid” will be reduced to 2mm by buying COTS parts.}}
    \label{fig:enclosure}
\end{figure}

\subsection{\DIFadd{Internal Layout}}

\DIFadd{The internal layout of the \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
experiment is arranged to maintain a compact configuration and minimize the length of the airflow path between the pressurized chamber and the compressor.
Electronic control hardware is mounted along the inner bottom of the enclosure, providing physical isolation between electrical components and the pressurized air system.
This configuration ensures efficient airflow through the chamber while maintaining accessibility for integration and servicing.
}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
    \centering
    \includegraphics[width=0.8\textwidth]{0_images/figures/tech_drawing_6.png}
    \caption{\DIFaddFL{Drawing of the internal layout.}}
    \label{fig:int_layout}

\end{figure}

\subsection{\DIFadd{Pressurized Measurement Chamber}}

\DIFadd{The core element of the experiment is a small pressurized chamber that houses the K96 sensor used for the measurements. The chamber has internal dimensions of approximately $38 \times 33 \times 45$ }\DIFaddend mm and a wall thickness of \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{15 mmcontaining the K96 sensor, as shown in \fref{fig:CAD}.
The total mass of the mechanical structure, excluding internal components, is approximately 800 g. }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{7 mm. It will be machined from aluminium by the \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
team at Uppsala University.
}

\DIFadd{The chamber is sealed using a copper gasket to ensure reliable sealing under elevated pressure conditions and temperature changes. Copper gaskets were selected due to their ability to provide a robust metal-to-metal seal capable of maintaining integrity at high pressure differentials.
}\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The internal pressurised chamber operates at pressures of up to 5 bar , while }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The chamber is designed to minimize internal volume while providing sufficient space for the sensor and the necessary airflow path. Reducing the internal volume proportionally lowers the airflow rate required to exchange the chamber atmosphere, which improves the overall performance of the experiment.
}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
    \centering
    \includegraphics[width=0.45\textwidth]{0_images/figures/render2.png}
    \includegraphics[width=0.45\textwidth]{0_images/figures/render1.png}
    \caption{\DIFaddFL{Renders of the pressurized chamber.}}
    \label{fig:pressure_render}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
    \centering
    \includegraphics[width=0.45\textwidth]{0_images/figures/tech_drawing_2.png}
    \includegraphics[width=0.45\textwidth]{0_images/figures/tech_drawing_4.png}
    \caption{\DIFaddFL{Technical drawings of the pressurized chamber.}}
    \label{fig:pressure_drawing}
\end{figure}

\subsection{\DIFadd{Pump System Architecture}}\label{sec: pump system arch}

\DIFadd{The \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
experiment utilizes a multi-stage air circulation system to maintain a controlled internal pressure while ensuring a continuous exchange of air within the measurement chamber.
}

\textbf{\DIFadd{System Operation:}}

\begin{enumerate}
    \item \DIFadd{Pre-heating: Ambient intake air is pre-heated before entering the vacuum stage to prevent condensation or freezing within the system components.
    }\item \DIFadd{Vacuum Stage: Two diaphragm vacuum pumps operate continuously from launch up to an altitude of 22 km. These pumps supply the secondary stage with air at approximately atmospheric pressure ($\approx$ 1 bar). Since the volumetric flow rate decreases with decreasing intake pressure, the pumps will operate at higher settings at higher altitudes.
}

    \item \DIFadd{Intercooling: To manage thermal loads generated by compression, the tubing connecting the vacuum pumps to the piston compressor serves as a passive intercooler.
    }\item \DIFadd{Compression Stage: A piston compressor increases the airflow pressure to a maximum of 3 bar before it enters the measurement chamber.
    }\item \DIFadd{Pressure Regulation: The internal chamber pressure is maintained by a passive outflow valve equipped with a shutter mechanism. This valve regulates the exhaust flow rate to the external environment.
    }\item \DIFadd{Monitoring: Integrated pressure and temperature sensors are situated within the tubing between compression stages to provide real-time performance data and ensure stable operation.
}\end{enumerate}

%DIF > % ADD FIGURE %%

\textbf{\DIFadd{Compressor Design Considerations:}} \DIFadd{Two primary design methodologies are being evaluated for the compression stage:
}

\begin{enumerate}
    \item \DIFadd{Continuous Low-Flow Operation: Utilizing a compressor capable of maintaining a continuous, very low flow rate to match the chamber's exchange requirements.
    }\item \DIFadd{Intermittent Buffered Operation: Utilizing a higher flow rate compressor operated in duty cycles. This configuration requires a 1 bar buffer tank between pressurisation stages to accumulate air from the vacuum stage. The compressor activates to deplete the tank and deactivates once the tank pressure reaches a lower threshold.
}\end{enumerate}

\DIFadd{The nominal operating pressure inside the chamber is expected to reach approximately 3 bar above perfect vacuum. At float altitude, }\DIFaddend the external ambient pressure \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{at float altitude can be as low as }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{may decrease to }\DIFaddend approximately 10 mbar, resulting in a \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{maximum }\DIFdelend pressure differential of approximately \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{5 bar which }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{3 bar across the chamber walls. This pressure differential }\DIFaddend is accounted for in the structural design \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{of the chamber}\DIFaddend .

The \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{outer housing has one detachable wall fastened with four M2x10 screws, allowing access during integration and testing. The housing includes openings for air inlet and outlet for the pressurisation system, as well as internal mounting provisions for electrical components}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{pressure between the vacuum pumps and the compressor is expected to remain close to atmospheric pressure ($\approx$ 1 bar) during normal operation in order to match expected compressor efficiency.
}

\DIFadd{Temperature conditions at float altitude will require the implementation of pre-heating of the intake air before the vacuum stage to prevent condensation or freezing within the system. Additionally, pressure sensors will be placed between compression stages to monitor system performance and ensure stable pressure control during operation.
}

%DIF >  \subsection{In-line Sensing and Environmental Monitoring}

%DIF >  To ensure the operational integrity of the gas handling system and to facilitate real-time performance analysis, the \gls{mirage} experiment incorporates an integrated sensing suite within the tube circuit. This monitoring architecture is essential for validating the state of the air as it transitions through the various compression and thermal management stages.

%DIF >  \begin{enumerate}
%DIF >      \item Pressure Sensing: High-precision pressure sensors are situated within the tubing between the diaphragm vacuum pumps and the piston compressor. These sensors monitor the inter-stage pressure to ensure that the vacuum pumps, operating continuously up to 22 km, maintain the required 1 bar supply pressure for the compressor.
%DIF >      \item Temperature Sensing: Thermal sensors are embedded directly into the flow path to monitor the effectiveness of the pre-heating and intercooling mechanisms. Monitoring the air temperature post-heating is critical to verify that the intake air has reached a safe threshold before entering the pump heads and K96 sensor chamber, thereby preventing damage from cold or heat
%DIF >  \end{enumerate}

\subsection{\DIFadd{Pump and Fluid Handling Technologies}}

\DIFadd{Small gas circulation and sampling systems used in atmospheric sensing instruments typically rely on compact electrically driven pumps to move air through measurement chambers and sensors. Several pump technologies are commonly used in portable gas analysis systems, including diaphragm pumps, piston compressors, rotary vane pumps, and scroll pumps. Each technology offers different advantages in terms of pressure capability, size, reliability, and maintenance requirements.
}

\DIFadd{Diaphragm pumps are widely used in environmental monitoring and portable gas sampling instruments. These pumps operate by oscillating a flexible diaphragm using an electric motor, creating alternating suction and compression cycles. Because the gas is hermetically separated the mechanical drive components by the diaphragm, diaphragm pumps operate oil-free and are resistant to contamination. This makes them particularly suitable for experiments involving sensitive sensors or atmospheric gas sampling. Furthermore, diaphragm pumps are compact, lightweight, and tolerant of condensation in the airflow, which is expected in the \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
experiment due to low external temperatures at float altitude.
}

\DIFadd{Piston compressors are commonly used when higher pressures are required. These pumps use a reciprocating piston to compress air within a cylinder, allowing significantly higher pressure ratios than typical diaphragm pumps. However, piston compressors generally contain more moving mechanical parts and may be more sensitive to contamination or thermal effects. For this reason, piston compressors are often used in series with diaphragm pumps in small air circulation systems, where the diaphragm pumps provide initial airflow and the compressor increases the pressure to the required level.
}

\DIFadd{Other pump technologies, such as rotary vane pumps and scroll pumps, are frequently used in laboratory vacuum systems. While these technologies can achieve significantly lower pressures and higher pumping speeds, they typically require lubrication, larger mechanical assemblies, and higher power consumption. Due to these characteristics, they are generally unsuitable for compact balloon payload experiments such as \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
, where mass, power consumption, and system simplicity are critical design constraints}\DIFaddend .

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The internal pressurised chambercontaining the K96 sensor includes dedicated interfaces for air inlet, air outlet aligned with the openings in the external housing, and electrical feedthroughs.
One wall of the chamber is detachable and fastened with four M2x10 screws to allow sensor installation and servicing}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Based on this comparison, diaphragm pumps were selected as the primary airflow drivers in the \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
experiment due to their oil-free operation, compact size, reliability, and resistance to condensation. A piston compressor is used downstream of the diaphragm pumps to achieve the required pressurization of the measurement chamber}\DIFaddend .

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The pressurisation system is based on a }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \subsection{\DIFadd{Tubing and Flow Control Components}}

\DIFadd{Gas flow regulation in compact atmospheric sensing instruments is traditionally achieved through the use of miniature solenoid or needle valves. Solenoid valves are often preferred for their rapid response times and ability to provide high-precision, electronically controlled flow regulation within automated systems.
However, for the \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
experiment, the design has been optimized to utilize a passive outflow valve equipped with a mechanical shutter. This shift to a passive regulation system is engineered to maintain the required internal chamber pressure of approximately 3 bar by modulating the exhaust flow rate (hole size) based on the pressure differential encountered during the flight profile. In addition the usage of a shutter-based passive mechanism rather than an active solenoid, the system achieves greater mechanical simplicity and safety if the ballon would fall into the water.
The final selection of the hole and the shutter's mechanical properties is based on ensuring a stable airflow path that accommodates the continuous operation of the upstream diaphragm pumps up to the 22 km altitude threshold.
}

\subsection{\DIFadd{Tubing and Fluid Connections}}

\DIFadd{The airflow between the pumps, compressor, and pressurized measurement chamber is transported through flexible tubing. In compact gas circulation systems, tubing connections are typically achieved using barbed fittings, compression fittings, or push-to-connect pneumatic fittings.
}

\DIFadd{Barbed fittings are commonly used with flexible tubing materials such as silicone or polyurethane, where the tubing is pressed onto the fitting and secured through friction or hose clamps. Compression fittings provide a more robust and leak-tight connection and are frequently used in higher-pressure gas systems. Push-to-connect fittings are widely used in pneumatic systems due to their ease of installation and reliable sealing.
}

\DIFadd{For the \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
experiment, the tubing connections will be selected to ensure leak-tight operation at pressures up to approximately 3 bar while maintaining compatibility with the chosen tubing material and the compact geometry of the experimental setup. Particular attention will be given to minimizing leakage and dead volumes in the system to maintain stable pressure control and reliable airflow through the measurement chamber.
}

\DIFadd{In alignment with the experiment's thermal management requirements, the intake tube lines will be integrated with high-conductivity copper windings to facilitate efficient heat transfer between the enclosure and the vacuum pump interface. This thermal exchange mechanism is designed to rapidly elevate the temperature of the intake air, ensuring the fluid stream remains within the pump's safe operational range. This will also be the case between compressor and the chamber as the heat created by compression could affect the quality of the study. This proactively mitigates the risk of mechanical failure or structural damage to the diaphragm components caused by the extreme low-temperature environment encountered during the ascent to 22 km and high temperatures after compression.
}

\subsection{\DIFadd{Pumps}}

\DIFadd{The air circulation system utilizes commercially available miniature medical pumps. The vacuum pumps are compact DC diaphragm pumps capable of generating the suction required to draw air into the system at 10 mbar. Two pumps are used to provide sufficient airflow at 1 bar for the compressor and to enhance system robustness.
}

\DIFadd{The compressor is a small DC piston air }\DIFaddend pump used to increase the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{internal chamber pressure and an electronically controlled valve used to enable controlled flushing of the chamber.
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{pressure of the air entering the pressurized chamber. Both components were selected based on their cost, compact size, low mass, and compatibility with the power constraints of the BEXUS payload system.
}\DIFaddend 

\DIFaddbegin \subsection{\DIFadd{Structural Considerations}}

\DIFadd{The mechanical structure is designed with sufficient strength and safety margin to withstand internal pressure differentials exceeding the maximum expected value of approximately 3 bar between the pressurized chamber and the external environment.
The pressurized chamber is manufactured from solid machined aluminium with a wall thickness of 7 mm. This thickness provides a structural safety factor far greater than 2 relative to the maximum expected pressure differential, accounting for uncertainties in material properties, manufacturing tolerances, and thermal stresses.
The outer aluminium enclosure provides mechanical protection and structural support for the internal components. A copper gasket is used to ensure reliable sealing and minimize the risk of leakage during operation.
The internal layout maintains a compact configuration while ensuring that mechanical loads generated by the pumps, tubing, and mounting hardware are safely transferred to the enclosure structure.
}

\DIFadd{A preliminary mass budget of the \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
experiment was derived from the SolidWorks CAD assembly model. The estimated mass distribution of the main structural, fluid handling, electronic, and fastening components is summarized in \tref{tab:mass_budget}. Smaller components such as fasteners and connectors are included to provide a realistic estimate of the total system mass.
}

\subsection{\DIFadd{Component Procurement Summary}}

\gls{mirage} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
experiment.
}

\DIFadd{The \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\gls{cots} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
components include the aluminium enclosure, diaphragm vacuum pumps, piston compressor, shutter valve, tubing, and standard fasteners. These components were selected in order to reduce manufacturing complexity, cost, and lead time.
}

\DIFadd{Custom-manufactured components include the pressurized measurement chamber (chamber body and lid) and several structural mounting elements such as pump holders, valve holders, and supporting brackets. These parts are machined from aluminium at Uppsala University to meet the structural and pressure requirements of the experiment.
}
